## Reply 514 — participant_203 · 2026-04-24 · post-31250733

Idea for a scheme/mini story cycle: So you are (or an AI ruler is) a somewhat greedy and rather broke king. You have a strong hook on your HoF, and there is a very rich holy order in your realm, whose leader is preferably lacking in skullduggery. It would be very cash money (literally) if you could attempt (perks permitting) to fabricate a charge of heresy against the holy order, so you can disband the order, execute its membership and take their land and money. Reward (if successfull): money, dread. Cost: tyranny, level of fame or two, level of devotion or two if the charge of heresy doesn't stick. Full credit to Phillip IV the Fair of France.

"Empire" tier titles have their purposes - firstly allowing large realms to exist more practically, and let kings be vassalised by suitably powerful other kings - or cases where a "king" title is historically the title of a junior king or the heir of a more powerful one; and secondly giving guidance for the AI and newer players where to expand after securing a king title. Besides, there are *at least* two Christian (this being the religion that both Catholicism and Orthodoxy belong to) Empires, which although they had frictions, both co-existed. Rome itself is a hegemony now, above Empires. Britannia, Francia, and Hispania have historical precedent as Empires as previous splinters of the Roman Empire, and Britannia in particular makes sense as a "High King" type position to allow, for example, the temporary subjugation of Scotland, as well as the continued ambition to rule the whole archipelego under one crown. Scandinavia as an "empire" doesn't have to be an echo of Rome, and can easily look to being an empire of the lands beyond the borders of Rome, uniting the 4/5 kingdoms in the area in a way that's not practical under multiple king titles. A christian Persia could draw its legitimacy as an Empire from the previous Iranian entities; and could rely on the concept of "King of (or over) Kings" for its title and positioning.

I do agree : Empire titles do have their purpose, to make some kings above the others. However, I feel like those Emperor titles should have another name : eg "king of the kings" (or simply "King" and shift the whole hierarchy : King->Duke, Duke-> Count, Count->Viscount). In this way, only a "king of the kings" could aspire to get recognised as Emperor by the Faith authority. Of course, the Faith authority they refer to can be a different. And both side will struggle with the other side to be the real true Emperor on earth (or within Christendom) So did the German and the Byzantines from Charlemagne. In the end, one side can win ; or maybe one of them will decide to declare a schism to break the religion in two parts and let room for two distinct Emperors... I do have the feeling that what Paradox is announcing here lets room for such mechanics... However, Emperors were not mentioned so I am keeping fingers crossed.

I'll take "High King" as a title for Britannia or Scandinavia. Although at least one Anglo-Saxon king tried "Imperator" as a title, but it didn't last. Alas, we've already got Anglo-Saxon dukes trying to call themselves kings (listed as petty king in a few places) when independent, and Duke wasn't used early on in England, with the high ranking land title being Earl for a significant period (equivalent to Jarl...).

## Reply 521 — participant_298 · 2026-04-29 · post-31259501

I think military orders should be reworked. For example, you give some undeveloped land to military order, and you can wait patiently to build itself through time, or help it with buildings, like with manor. Depending on the buildings, military order gets those type of units and characteristics that help it on the battlefield. So basically one military order shouldnt have more than a few hundred troops, but they could be elite punch on the field. But there is a catch, you cannot hire military order across the entire map, it needs to be in your vicinity. And how to limit them - simple, only one military order can be built in de jure kingdom territory. If hostile religion ruler takes it, it becomes abandoned site, which you can rebuilt into your own faith military order, or convert it into other type of settlement.

## Reply 522 — participant_283 · 2026-04-29 · post-31259703

In that one survey almost a year ago, one of the proposed future DLC was titled Feudalism and Crusades. And among its possible features, it included Holy Orders. So, if they will ever receive a significant rework or be made playable, then it will be with that expansion (probably next year?). Hence it's not surprising to me that they won't be playable in By God Alone.
